          <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:114px; top:308px">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_Ceuta.svg">
            <img alt="Flag Ceuta.svg" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="17" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flag_Ceuta.svg/25px-Flag_Ceuta.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flag_Ceuta.svg/38px-Flag_Ceuta.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Flag_Ceuta.svg/50px-Flag_Ceuta.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>

      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       , an
       <b>
        autonomous community
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         comunidad autónoma
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="eu">
         autonomia erkidegoa
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         comunitat autònoma
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="gl">
         comunidade autónoma
        </span>
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a first-level
       <a href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Spain" title="Political divisions of Spain">
        political and administrative division
       </a>
       , created in accordance with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">
        Spanish constitution of 1978
       </a>
       , with the aim of guaranteeing limited autonomy of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">
        nationalities and regions
       </a>
       that make up Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-eso-2">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art2_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-art2-3">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art143_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-art143-4">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Spain is not a
       <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">
        federation
       </a>
       , but a highly
       <a href="/wiki/Decentralization" title="Decentralization">
        decentralized
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsis145_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsis145-5">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">
        unitary state
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-eso-2">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While sovereignty is vested in the nation as a whole, represented in the central institutions of government, the nation has asymmetrically
       <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">
        devolved
       </a>
       power to the communities, which, in turn, exercise their right to self-government within the limits set forth in the constitution and their autonomous statutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-eso-2">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some scholars have referred to the resulting system as a federal system in all but name or a "federation without federalism".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain_Xavier_Arbós_Marín_page_375_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spain_Xavier_Arbós_Marín_page_375-7">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are 17 autonomous communities and two autonomous cities that are collectively known as "
       <b>
        autonomies
       </b>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [i]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The two autonomous cities have the right to become autonomous communities, but neither has yet used this right. This unique framework of territorial administration is known as the "
       <b>
        State of Autonomies
       </b>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [ii]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The autonomous communities are governed according to the constitution and their own organic laws known as
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statutes of Autonomy
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [iii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which contain all the competences that they assume. Since devolution was intended to be asymmetrical in nature,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanja_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tanja-11">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the scope of competences vary for each community, but all have the same parliamentary structure.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eso_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-eso-2">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1022" data-file-width="1144" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg/350px-Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg/525px-Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg/700px-Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Espa%C3%B1a1757.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A map of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberia" title="Iberia">
          Iberia
         </a>
         in 1757
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Spain is a diverse country made up of several different regions with varying economic and social structures, as well as different languages and historical, political and cultural traditions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-villar_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-villar-12">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shabad_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-shabad-13">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the entire Spanish territory was united under one crown in 1479 this was not a process of national homogenization or amalgamation. The constituent territories—be it crowns, kingdoms, principalities or dominions—retained much of their former institutional existence,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morenopaper_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-morenopaper-14">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including limited legislative, judicial or fiscal autonomy. These territories also exhibited a variety of local customs, laws, languages and currencies until the mid nineteenth century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morenopaper_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-morenopaper-14">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 18th century onwards, the Bourbon kings and the government tried to establish a more centralized regime. Leading figures of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Enlightenment" title="Spanish Enlightenment">
        Spanish Enlightenment
       </a>
       advocated for the building of a Spanish nation beyond the internal territorial boundaries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morenopaper_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-morenopaper-14">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This culminated in 1833, when Spain was
       <a href="/wiki/1833_territorial_division_of_Spain" title="1833 territorial division of Spain">
        divided
       </a>
       into 49 (now 50)
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">
        provinces
       </a>
       , which served mostly as transmission belts for policies developed in Madrid.
      </p>
      <p>
       However, unlike in other European countries such as France, where regional languages were spoken in rural areas or less developed regions, two important regional languages of Spain were spoken in some of the most industrialized areas,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jackson_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jackson-15">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which, moreover, enjoyed higher levels of prosperity, in addition to having their own cultures and historical consciousness. These were the
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">
        Basque Country
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreno112_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-moreno112-17">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This gave rise to
       <a href="/wiki/Peripheral_nationalism" title="Peripheral nationalism">
        peripheral nationalisms
       </a>
       along with
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nationalism" title="Spanish nationalism">
        Spanish nationalism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Therefore, economic and social changes that had produced a national cultural unification in France had the opposite effect in Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As such, Spanish history since the late 19th century has been shaped by a dialectical struggle between Spanish nationalism and peripheral nationalisms,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreno98_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-moreno98-19">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       mostly in Catalonia and the Basque Country, and to a lesser degree in
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In a response to Catalan demands, limited autonomy was granted to Catalonia in 1913, only to be abolished in 1920. It was granted again in 1932 during the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">
        Second Spanish Republic
       </a>
       , when the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalitat_of_Catalonia" title="Generalitat of Catalonia">
        Generalitat
       </a>
       , Catalonia's mediaeval institution of government, was restored. The constitution of 1931 envisaged a territorial division for all Spain in "autonomous regions", which was never fully attained—only Catalonia, the Basque Country and Galicia had approved "
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statutes of Autonomy
       </a>
       "—the process being thwarted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       that broke out in 1936, and the victory of the rebel Nationalist forces under
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Francisco Franco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francoism" title="Francoism">
        Franco's dictatorial regime
       </a>
       , centralism was most forcefully enforced as a way of preserving the "unity of the Spanish nation".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Peripheral nationalism, along with communism and atheism were regarded by his regime as the main threats.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His attempts to fight separatism with heavy-handed but sporadic repression,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shabad_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-shabad-13">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and his often severe suppression of language and regional identities
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shabad_13-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-shabad-13">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       backfired: the demands for democracy became intertwined with demands for the recognition of a pluralistic vision of the Spanish nationhood.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreno78_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-moreno78-20">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When Franco died in 1975, Spain entered into a phase of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">
        transition towards democracy
       </a>
       . The most difficult task of the newly democratically elected
       <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">
        Cortes Generales
       </a>
       (the Spanish Parliament) in 1977 acting as a Constituent Assembly was to transition from a unitary centralized state into a decentralized state
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colomer_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-colomer-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in a way that would satisfy the demands of the peripheral nationalists.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mundo_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mundo-22">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portero_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-portero-23">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The then
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">
        Prime Minister of Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Adolfo Suárez">
        Adolfo Suárez
       </a>
       , met with
       <a href="/wiki/Josep_Tarradellas" title="Josep Tarradellas">
        Josep Tarradellas
       </a>
       , president of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalitat_of_Catalonia" title="Generalitat of Catalonia">
        Generalitat of Catalonia
       </a>
       in exile. An agreement was made so that the Generalitat would be restored and limited competencies would be transferred while the constitution was still being written. Shortly after, the government allowed the creation of "assemblies of members of parliament" integrated by deputies and senators of the different territories of Spain, so that they could constitute "pre-autonomic regimes" for their regions as well.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Fathers_of_the_Constitution" title="Fathers of the Constitution">
        Fathers of the Constitution
       </a>
       had to strike a balance between the opposing views of Spain—on the one hand, the centralist view inherited from Franco's regime,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colomer_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-colomer-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on the other hand
       <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">
        federalism
       </a>
       and a pluralistic view of Spain as a "nation of nations";
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsis2_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsis2-24">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       between a uniform decentralization of entities with the same competencies and an asymmetrical structure that would distinguish the nationalities. Peripheral nationalist parties wanted a multinational state with a federal or confederal model, whereas the governing
       <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Democratic_Centre_(Spain)" title="Union of the Democratic Centre (Spain)">
        Union of the Democratic Centre
       </a>
       (UCD) and the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Alliance_(Spain)" title="People's Alliance (Spain)">
        People's Alliance
       </a>
       (AP) wanted minimum decentralization; the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">
        Spanish Socialist Workers' Party
       </a>
       (PSOE) was sympathetic to a federal system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the end, the constitution, published and ratified in 1979, found a balance in recognizing the existence of "nationalities and regions" in Spain, within the "indissoluble unity of the Spanish nation". In order to manage the tensions present in the Spanish transition to democracy, the drafters of the current Spanish constitution avoided giving labels such as 'federal' to the territorial arrangements,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while enshrining in the constitution the right to autonomy or self-government of the "nationalities and regions", through a process of asymmetric
       <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">
        devolution
       </a>
       of power to the "autonomous communities" that were to be created.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution_of_1978">
        Constitution of 1978
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Constitution of 1978">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">
        Spanish Constitution of 1978
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The starting point in the territorial organization of Spain was the second article of the constitution,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which reads:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        The Constitution is based on the indissoluble unity of the Spanish Nation, the common and indivisible homeland of all Spaniards; it recognizes and guarantees the right to self-government of the nationalities and regions of which it is composed and the solidarity among them all.
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Second Article of the Spanish Constitution of 1978
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       The constitution was rather ambiguous on how this was to take place.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colomer_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-colomer-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nunez_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nunez-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It does not define, detail, or impose the structure of the state;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portero_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-portero-23">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it does not tell the difference between "nation" and "nationality"; and it does not specify which are the "nationalities" and which are the "regions", or the territories they comprise.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rather than imposing, it
       <i>
        enables
       </i>
       a process towards a decentralized structure based on the exercise that these "nationalities and regions" would make of the right to self-government that they were granted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As such, the outcome of this exercise was not predictable
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barberia_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-barberia-31">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and its construction was deliberately open-ended;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frans_16-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-frans-16">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the constitution only created a process for an eventual
       <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">
        devolution
       </a>
       , but it was voluntary in nature: the "nationalities and regions" themselves had the option of choosing to attain self-government or not.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsis143_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsis143-32">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In order to exercise this right, the constitution established an open process whereby the "nationalities and regions" could be constituted as "autonomous communities". First, it recognized the pre-existing 50
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">
        provinces of Spain
       </a>
       , a territorial division of the liberal centralizing regime of the 19th century created for purely administrative purposes (it also recognized the
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">
        municipalities
       </a>
       that integrated the provinces). These provinces would serve as the building blocks and constituent parts of the autonomous communities. The constitution stipulated that the following could be constituted as autonomous communities:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article143_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-article143-33">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Two or more adjacent provinces with common historical, cultural and economic characteristics.
       </li>
       <li>
        Insular territories.
       </li>
       <li>
        A single province with a "historical regional identity".
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       It also allowed for exceptions to the above criteria, in that the Spanish Parliament could:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article143_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-article143-33">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Authorize, in the nation's interest, the constitution of an autonomous community even if it was a single province without a historical regional identity.
       </li>
       <li>
        Authorize or grant autonomy to entities or territories that were not provinces.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The constitution also established two "routes" to accede to autonomy. The "fast route" or "fast track",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nunez_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nunez-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       also called the "exception",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was established in article 151, and was implicitly reserved for the three "historical nationalities"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanja_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tanja-11">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsisDT2_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsisDT2-34">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —the Basque Country, Catalonia and Galicia—in that the very strict requirements to opt for this route were waived via the second transitory disposition for those territories that had approved a "Statute of Autonomy" during the Second Spanish Republic
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsisDT2_34-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsisDT2-34">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (otherwise, the constitution required the approval of three-fourths of the municipalities involved whose population would sum up at least the majority of the electoral census of each province, and required the ratification through a
       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">
        referendum
       </a>
       with the affirmative vote of the absolute majority of the electoral census of each province—that is, of all registered citizens, not only of those who would vote).
      </p>
      <p>
       The constitution also explicitly established that the institutional framework for these communities would be a
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentary system
       </a>
       , with a Legislative Assembly elected by
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">
        universal suffrage
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">
        cabinet
       </a>
       or "council of government", a president of such a council, elected by the Assembly, and a High Court of Justice. They were also granted a maximum level of devolved competencies.
      </p>
      <p>
       The "slow route" or "slow track",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nunez_29-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-nunez-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       also called the "norm",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was established in article 143. This route could be taken—via the first transitory disposition—by the "pre-autonomic regimes" that had been constituted in 1978, while the constitution was still being drafted, if approved by two-thirds of all municipalities involved whose population would sum up to at least the majority of the electoral census of each province or insular territory. These communities would assume limited competences during a provisional period of 5 years, after which they could assume further competences, upon negotiation with the central government. However, the constitution did not explicitly establish an institutional framework for these communities. They could have established a parliamentary system like the "historical nationalities", or they could have not assumed any legislative powers and simply established mechanisms for the administration of the competences they were granted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Once the autonomous communities were created, Article 145 prohibits the "federation of autonomous communities". This was understood as any agreement between communities that would produce an alteration to the political and territorial equilibrium that would cause a confrontation between different blocks of communities, an action incompatible with the principle of solidarity and the unity of the nation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gonzalez_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gonzalez-35">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The so-called "additional" and "transitory" dispositions of the constitution allowed for some exceptions to the above-mentioned framework. In terms of territorial organization, the fifth transitory disposition established that the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">
        Melilla
       </a>
       , Spanish exclaves located on the northern coast of Africa, could be constituted as "autonomous communities" if the absolute majority of the members of their city councils would agree on such a motion, and with the approval of the Spanish Parliament, which would exercise its prerogatives to grant autonomy to other entities besides provinces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transitorias_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-transitorias-36">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In terms of the scope of competences, the first additional disposition recognized the historical rights of the "chartered" territories,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lurraldeak_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lurraldeak-37">
         [iv]
        </a>
       </sup>
       namely the Basque-speaking provinces, which were to be updated in accordance with the constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adicionales_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-adicionales-38">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This recognition would allow them to establish a financial "
       <a href="/wiki/Communities_of_chartered_regime" title="Communities of chartered regime">
        chartered regime
       </a>
       " whereby they would not only have independence to manage their own finances, like all other communities, but to have their own public financial ministries with the ability to levy and collect all taxes. In the rest of the communities, all taxes are levied and collected by or for the central government and then redistributed among all.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomic_pacts">
        Autonomic pacts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Autonomic pacts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Statutes of Autonomy of the Basque Country and Catalonia were sanctioned by the Spanish Parliament on 18 December 1979. The position of the party in government, the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Democratic_Centre_(Spain)" title="Union of the Democratic Centre (Spain)">
        Union of the Democratic Centre
       </a>
       (UCD), was that only the three "historical nationalities" would assume full competences, while the rest would accede to autonomy via article 143, assuming fewer powers and perhaps not even establishing institutions of government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rebollo_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rebollo-39">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was firmly opposed by the representatives of
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       , who demanded for their region the maximum level of competences granted to the "nationalities".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After a massive rally in support of autonomy, a referendum was organized for Andalusia to attain autonomy through the strict requirements of article 151, or the "fast route"—with UCD calling for abstention, and the main party in opposition in Parliament, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">
        Spanish Socialist Workers' Party
       </a>
       (PSOE) calling for a vote in favour.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These requirements were not met, as in one of the eight provinces,
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Almer%C3%ADa" title="Province of Almería">
        Almería
       </a>
       , votes in favour—although the majority—did not amount to half of the electoral census as required. Yet, in general, the results of the referendum had been clear and unequivocal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After several months of discussion, the then prime minister of Spain,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Adolfo Suárez">
        Adolfo Suárez
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Spain)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Spain)">
        leader of the opposition
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Felipe González">
        Felipe González
       </a>
       , reached an agreement to resolve the Andalusian issue, whereby the Parliament approved an amendment to the law that regulated referendums, and used a prerogative of article 144c of the constitution, both actions which combined would allow Andalusia to take the fast route. They also agreed that no other region would take the "fast route", but that all regions would establish a parliamentary system with all institutions of government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This opened a phase that was dubbed as
       <i>
        café para todos
       </i>
       , "coffee for all".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanja_11-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-tanja-11">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This agreement was eventually put into writing in July 1981 in what has been called the "first autonomic pacts".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nunez_29-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-nunez-29">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       These "autonomic pacts"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [v]
        </a>
       </sup>
       filled in the gap left by the open character of the constitution. Among other things:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acuerdos_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-acuerdos-41">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        They described the final outline of the territorial division of Spain, with the specific number and name of the autonomous communities to be created.
       </li>
       <li>
        They restricted the "fast-route" to the "historical nationalities" and Andalusia; all the rest had to take the "slow-route".
       </li>
       <li>
        They established that all autonomous communities would have institutions of government within a parliamentary system.
       </li>
       <li>
        They set up a deadline for all the remaining communities to be constituted: 1 February 1983.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In the end, 17 autonomous communities were created:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Andalusia, and the three "historical nationalities"—the Basque Country, Catalonia and Galicia—took the "fast-route" and assumed the maximum level of competences immediately; the rest took the "slow route".
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">
         Aragon
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Castilla-La_Mancha" title="Castilla-La Mancha">
         Castilla-La Mancha
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">
         Castile and León
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">
         Extremadura
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
         Valencian Community
        </a>
        acceded to autonomy as communities integrated by two or more provinces with common historical, economic and cultural characteristics.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
         Balearic Islands
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
         Canary Islands
        </a>
        acceded to autonomy as insular territories, the latter integrated by two provinces.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
         Principality of Asturias
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">
         Cantabria
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/La_Rioja_(Spain)" title="La Rioja (Spain)">
         La Rioja
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">
         Murcia
        </a>
        acceded to autonomy as single provinces with historical identity (also called "uniprovincial" autonomous communities).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">
         Navarre
        </a>
        , as a single province, acceded to autonomy through the recognition, update and improvement of its historical and local "law" (charters; Spanish
        <i>
         fueros
        </i>
        ), and as such, it is known as a "chartered community".
       </li>
       <li>
        The province of Madrid, home to the national capital, was removed from Castilla-La Mancha (formerly
        <a href="/wiki/New_Castile_(Spain)" title="New Castile (Spain)">
         New Castile
        </a>
        ), to which it previously belonged, and constituted as a single-province autonomous community in the "national interest", the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Madrid" title="Community of Madrid">
          Community of Madrid
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Special provisions were made for the Valencian Community and the Canary Islands in that, although they took the "slow route", through the subsequent approval of specific organic laws, they were to assume the maximum level of competences in less than 5 years, since they had started a process towards the "fast route" prior to the approval of the "autonomic pacts".
      </p>
      <p>
       On the other hand, Cantabria and La Rioja, although originally part of
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Castile" title="Old Castile">
        Old Castile
       </a>
       —and both originally included in the "pre-autonomic regime" of Castile and León—were granted autonomy as single provinces with historical identity, a move supported by the majority of their populations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clavero_30-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-clavero-30">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-garciaruiz_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-garciaruiz-42">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The "autonomic pacts" give both Cantabria and La Rioja the option of being incorporated into Castile and León in the future, and required that the Statutes of Autonomy of all three communities include such a provision.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acuerdos_41-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-acuerdos-41">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       León, a historical kingdom and historical region of Spain, once joined to
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Castile" title="Old Castile">
        Old Castile
       </a>
       to form Castile and León, was denied secession to be constituted as an autonomous community on its own right.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moreno66_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-moreno66-43">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Congreso_de_los_Diputados_(Espa%C3%B1a)_14.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/220px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/330px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/440px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Congreso_de_los_Diputados_(Espa%C3%B1a)_14.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Spanish Parliament, Congress of Deputies
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the second half of the 1980s, the central government seemed reluctant to transfer all competences to the "slow route" communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mundo_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mundo-22">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the five years set up by the constitution, all "slow route" communities demanded the maximum transfer guaranteed by the constitution. This led to what has been called the "second autonomic pacts" of 1992, between the then prime minister of Spain
       <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Felipe González">
        Felipe González
       </a>
       from PSOE and the leader of the opposition,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">
        José María Aznar
       </a>
       from the newly created
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
        People's Party
       </a>
       (PP) successor of the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Alliance_(Spain)" title="People's Alliance (Spain)">
        People's Alliance party
       </a>
       . Through these agreements new competences were transferred, with the reforms to many Statutes of Autonomy of the "slow-route" communities with the aim of equalizing them to the "fast route" communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mundo_22-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-mundo-22">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1995, the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">
        Melilla
       </a>
       were constituted as "autonomous cities" without legislative powers, but with an autonomous assembly
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="How can an autonomous assembly not have legislative powers? (October 2014)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       not subordinated to any other province or community.
      </p>
      <p>
       The creation of the autonomous communities was a diverse process, that started with the constitution, was normalized with the autonomic pacts and was completed with the Statutes of Autonomy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is, however, an ongoing process; further devolution—or even the return of transferred competences—is always a possibility. This has been evidenced in the 2000s, at the beginning with a wave of approval of new Statutes of Autonomy for many communities, and more recently with many considering the recentralization of some competences in the wake of the economic and financial crisis of 2008. Nonetheless Spain is now a highly decentralized country with a structure unlike any other, similar but not equal to a
       <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">
        federation
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       even though in many respects the country can be compared to countries which are undeniably federal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The unique resulting system is referred to as "Autonomous state", or more precisely "State of Autonomies".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colomer_21-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-colomer-21">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_state_of_affairs">
        Current state of affairs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Current state of affairs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       With the implementation of the Autonomous Communities, Spain went from being one of the most centralized countries in the
       <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">
        OECD
       </a>
       to being one of the most decentralized; in particular, it has been the country where the incomes and outcomes of the decentralized bodies (the Autonomous Communities) has grown the most, leading this rank in Europe by 2015 and being fifth among OECD countries in tax devolution (after Canada, Switzerland, the United States and Austria).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By means of the State of Autonomies implemented after the Spanish Constitution of 1978, Spain has been quoted to be "remarkable for the extent of the powers peacefully devolved over the past 30 years" and "an extraordinarily decentralized country", with the central government accounting for just 18% of public spending,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mallet_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mallet-47">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       38% for the regional governments, 13% for the local councils, and the remaining 31% for the
       <a href="/wiki/Social_insurance" title="Social insurance">
        social security system
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-economist.com-48">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In terms of personnel, by 2010 almost 1,350,000 people or 50.3% of the total
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_servants" title="Civil servants">
        civil servants
       </a>
       in Spain were employed by the autonomous communities;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       city and provincial councils accounted for 23.6% and those employees working for the central administration (police and military included) represented 22.2% of the total.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tensions_within_the_system">
        Tensions within the system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tensions within the system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Peripheral nationalism continues to play a key role in Spanish politics. Some peripheral nationalists view that there is a vanishing practical distinction between the terms "nationalities" and "regions",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keatings_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-keatings-51">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as more competences are transferred to all communities in roughly the same degree and as other communities have chosen to identify themselves as "nationalities". In fact, it has been argued that the establishment of the State of Autonomies "has led to the creation of "new regional identities",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-junco_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-junco-53">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and "invented communities".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-junco_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-junco-53">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;max-width:348px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG/180px-Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG/270px-Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG/360px-Fanals-Banc_P1150940.JPG 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BCN12-o.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="600" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BCN12-o.jpg/160px-BCN12-o.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BCN12-o.jpg/240px-BCN12-o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/BCN12-o.jpg/320px-BCN12-o.jpg 2x" width="160"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
         Pro-Catalan independence (left) and pro-Spanish demonstrations in
         <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
          Barcelona
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many in Galicia, the Basque Country, and Catalonia view their communities as "nations", not just "nationalities", and Spain as a "plurinational state" or a "nation of nations", and they have made demands for further devolution or secession.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2004 the Basque Parliament approved the
       <a href="/wiki/Ibarretxe_Plan" title="Ibarretxe Plan">
        Ibarretxe Plan
       </a>
       , whereby the Basque Country would approve a new Statute of Autonomy containing key provisions such as shared sovereignty with Spain, full independence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judiciary
       </a>
       , and the right to
       <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
        self-determination
       </a>
       , and assuming all competences except that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nationality_law" title="Spanish nationality law">
        Spanish nationality law
       </a>
       , defense, and monetary policy. The plan was rejected by the Spanish Parliament in 2005 and the situation has remained largely stable in that front so far.
      </p>
      <p>
       A particularly contentious point -especially in Catalonia- has been the one of fiscal tensions, with Catalan nationalists intensifying their demand for further financing over the last few years. In this regard, the new rules for fiscal decentralisation in force since 2011 already make Spain one of the most decentralised countries in the world also in budgetary and fiscal matters,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piketty_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Piketty-54">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the base for income tax split at 50/50 between the Spanish government and the regions (something unheard of in much bigger federal states such as Germany or the United States, which retain the income tax as an exclusively federal one).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piketty_54-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Piketty-54">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Besides, each region can also decide to set its own income tax bands and its own additional rates, higher or lower than the federal rates, with the corresponding income accruing to the region which no longer has to share it with other regions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piketty_54-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Piketty-54">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This current level of fiscal decentralisation has been regarded by economists such as
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Piketty" title="Thomas Piketty">
        Thomas Piketty
       </a>
       as troublesome since, in his view, "challenges the very idea of solidarity within the country and comes down to playing the regions against each other, which is particularly problematic when the issue is one of income tax as this is supposed to enable the reduction of inequalities between the richest and the poorest, over and above regional or professional identities".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Piketty_54-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Piketty-54">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_process_in_Catalonia">
        Independence process in Catalonia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Independence process in Catalonia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The severe
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Spain" title="Economy of Spain">
        economic crisis in Spain
       </a>
       that started in 2008 produced different reactions in the different communities. On one hand, some began to consider a return of some responsibilities to the central government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-abc-55">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while, on the other hand, in Catalonia debate on the fiscal deficit—Catalonia being one of the largest net contributors in taxes— led many who are not necessarily separatist but who are enraged by the financial deficit to support secession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nextstate_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nextstate-56">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianfabric_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guardianfabric-57">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 2012,
       <a href="/wiki/Artur_Mas" title="Artur Mas">
        Artur Mas
       </a>
       , then Catalonia's president, requested from the central government a new "fiscal agreement", with the possibility of giving his community powers equal to those of the communities of
       <a href="/wiki/Fuero" title="Fuero">
        chartered
       </a>
       regime, but prime minister
       <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">
        Mariano Rajoy
       </a>
       refused. Mas dissolved the Catalan Parliament, called for new elections, and promised to celebrate a referendum on independence within the next four years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rajoy's government declared that they would use all "legal instruments"—current legislation requires the central executive government or the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">
        Congress of Deputies
       </a>
       to call for or sanction a binding referendum—
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ley_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ley-59">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to block any such attempt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clash_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-clash-60">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Spanish Socialist Workers' Party and its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Catalonia" title="Socialist Party of Catalonia">
        counterpart in Catalonia
       </a>
       proposed to reopen the debate on the territorial organization of Spain, changing the constitution to create a true
       <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">
        federal system
       </a>
       to "better reflect the singularities" of Catalonia, as well as to modify the current taxation system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadofederal_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadofederal-61">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-navarro_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-navarro-62">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On Friday 27 of October 2017 the Catalan Parliament voted the independence of Catalonia; the result was 70 in favor, 10 against, 2 neither, with 53 representatives not present in protest. In the following days, the members of the Catalan government either fled or were imprisoned.
      </p>
      <p>
       One scholar summarises the current situation as follows
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        "
        <i>
         the autonomous state appears to have come full circle, with reproaches from all sides. According to some, it has not gone far enough and has failed to satisfy their aspirations for improved self-government. For others it has gone too far, fostering inefficiency or reprehensible linguistic policies
        </i>
        ".
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
         <a href="#cite_note-63">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_and_statutory_framework">
        Constitutional and statutory framework
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Constitutional and statutory framework">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The State of Autonomies, as established in Article 2 of the constitution, has been argued to be based on four principles: willingness to accede to autonomy, unity in diversity, autonomy but not sovereignty of the communities, and solidarity among them all.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carreras_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-carreras-64">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The structure of the autonomous communities is determined both by the devolution allowed by the constitution and the competences assumed in their respective Statutes of Autonomy. While the autonomic agreements and other laws have allowed for an "equalization" of all communities, differences still remain.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Statute_of_Autonomy">
        The Statute of Autonomy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Statute of Autonomy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statute of Autonomy
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Statute of Autonomy is the basic institutional law of the autonomous community or city, recognized by the Spanish constitution in article 147. It is approved by a parliamentary assembly representing the community, and then approved by the
       <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">
        Cortes Generales
       </a>
       , the Spanish Parliament, through an "Organic Law", requiring the favourable vote of the absolute majority of the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">
        Congress of Deputies
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       For communities that acceded to autonomy through the "fast route", a
       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">
        referendum
       </a>
       is required before it can be sanctioned by the Parliament. The Statutes of Autonomy must contain, at least, the name of the community, its territorial limits, the names, organization and seat of the institutions of government, the competences they assume and the principles for their bilingual policy, if applicable.
      </p>
      <p>
       The constitution establishes that all competences not explicitly assumed by the state—the central government—in the constitution, can be assumed by the autonomous community in their Statutes of Autonomy; but also, all competences not explicitly assumed by the autonomous community in their Statutes of Autonomy are automatically assumed by the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article143_33-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-article143-33">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In case of conflict, the constitution prevails.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article143_33-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-article143-33">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In case of disagreement, any administration can bring the case before the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Spain" title="Constitutional Court of Spain">
        Constitutional Court of Spain
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Institutional_organization">
        Institutional organization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Institutional organization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       All autonomous communities have a parliamentary system based on a division of powers comprising:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        A Legislative Assembly, whose members are elected by universal suffrage according to a system of
        <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">
         proportional representation
        </a>
        , in which all areas that integrate the territory are fairly represented
       </li>
       <li>
        A Council of Government, with executive and administrative powers, headed by a prime minister, whose official title is "president",
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lehendakari_65-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-lehendakari-65">
          [b]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
         <a href="#cite_note-66">
          [vi]
         </a>
        </sup>
        elected by the Legislative Assembly—usually the leader of the party or coalition with a majority in the Assembly—and nominated by the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" title="King of Spain">
         King of Spain
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        A High Court of Justice, hierarchically under the
        <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Spain" title="Supreme Court of Spain">
         Supreme Court of Spain
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oviedo03.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Oviedo03.jpg/220px-Oviedo03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Oviedo03.jpg/330px-Oviedo03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Oviedo03.jpg/440px-Oviedo03.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oviedo03.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Regional Palace, seat of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Junta" title="General Junta">
          General Junta
         </a>
         , the Parliament of the
         <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
          Principality of Asturias
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The majority of the communities have approved regional electoral laws within the limits set up by the laws for the entire country. Despite minor differences, all communities use
       <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">
        proportional representation
       </a>
       following
       <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D'Hondt method">
        D'Hondt method
       </a>
       ; all members of regional parliaments are elected for four-year terms, but the president of the community has the faculty to dissolve the legislature and call for early elections. Nonetheless in all communities, with the exception of the Basque Country, Catalonia, Galicia, and Andalusia, elections are celebrated the last Sunday of May every four years, concurrent with municipal elections in all Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carreras_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-carreras-64">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The names of the Council of Government and the Legislative Assembly vary between communities. In some autonomous communities, these institutions are restored historical bodies of government or representation of the previous kingdoms or regional entities within the Spanish Crown—like the Generalitat of Catalonia—while others are entirely new creations.
      </p>
      <p>
       In some, both the executive and the legislature, though constituting two separate institutions, are collectively identified with a single specific name. It should be noted, though, that a specific denomination may not refer to the same branch of government in all communities; for example,
       <i>
        junta
       </i>
       may refer to the executive office in some communities, to the legislature in others, or to the collective name of all branches of government in others.
      </p>
      <p>
       Given the ambiguity in the constitution that did not specify which territories were nationalities and which were regions, other territories, besides the implicit three "historical nationalities", have also chosen to identify themselves as nationalities, in accordance with their historical regional identity, such as Andalusia, Aragon, the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canary Islands
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="Autonomous_cities">
       </span>
       The two autonomous cities have more limited competences than autonomous communities, but more than other municipalities. The executive is exercised by a president, who is also the mayor of the city. In the same way, limited legislative power is vested in a local assembly in which the deputies are also the city councillors.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_powers">
        Legal powers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Legal powers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The autonomic agreements of 1982 and 1992 tried to equalize powers (competences) devolved to the 17 autonomous communities, within the limits of the constitution and the differences guaranteed by it. This has led to an "asymmetrical homogeneity".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perez_28-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-perez-28">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the words of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Spain" title="Constitutional Court of Spain">
        Constitutional Court of Spain
       </a>
       in its ruling of August 5, 1983, the autonomous communities are characterized by their "homogeneity and diversity...equal in their subordination to the constitutional order, in the principles of their representation in the Senate, in their legitimation before the Constitutional Court, and in that the differences between the distinct Statutes [of Autonomy] cannot imply economic or social privileges; however, they can be unequal with respect to the process to accede to autonomy and the concrete determination of the autonomic content of their Statute, and therefore, in their scope of competences. The autonomic regime is characterized by an equilibrium between homogeneity and diversity [...] Without the former there will be no unity or integration in the state's ensemble; without the latter, there would not be [a] true plurality and the capacity of self-government".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinopsis137_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sinopsis137-67">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1380" data-file-width="2200" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg/220px-Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg/330px-Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg/440px-Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ertzaintza_Volkswagen_Bilbao.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An
         <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">
          Ertzaintza
         </a>
         police car in the Basque Country
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The asymmetrical devolution is a unique characteristic of the territorial structure of Spain, in that the autonomous communities have a different range of devolved competences. These were based on what has been called in Spanish as
       <i>
        hechos diferenciales
       </i>
       , "differential facts" or "differential traits".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [vii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aja_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aja-69">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This expression refers to the idea that some communities have particular traits, with respect to Spain as a whole. In practice these traits are a native "language proper to their own territories" separate from Spanish, a particular financial regime or special civil rights expressed in a code, which generate a distinct political personality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aja_69-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aja-69">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These
       <i>
        hechos diferenciales
       </i>
       of their distinct political and historical personality are constitutionally and statutorily (i.e., in their Statutes of Autonomy) recognized in the exceptions granted to some of them and the additional competences they assume.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aja_69-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-aja-69">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Competences can be divided into three groups: exclusive to the central state or central government, shared competences, and devolved competences exclusive to the communities. Article 149 states which powers are exclusive to the central government: international relations, defense, administration of justice, commercial, criminal, civil, and labour legislation, customs, general finances and state debt, public health, basic legislation, and general coordination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All autonomous communities have the power to manage their own finances in the way they see fit, and are responsible for the administration of education—school and universities—health and social services and cultural and urban development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-howmuch_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-howmuch-70">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Yet there are differences as stipulated in their Statutes and the constitution:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carreras_64-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-carreras-64">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Aragon, the Balearic Islands, the Basque Country,
        <a href="/wiki/Civil_Code_of_Catalonia" title="Civil Code of Catalonia">
         Catalonia
        </a>
        , Galicia and the Valencian Community have a regional civil code
       </li>
       <li>
        Basque Country, Catalonia, and Navarre have their own police corps—the
        <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">
         Ertzaintza
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">
         Mossos d'Esquadra
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Foral" title="Policía Foral">
         Nafarroako Foruzaingoa
        </a>
        , respectively
       </li>
       <li>
        The Canary Islands have a special financial regime in virtue of its location as an overseas territories, while the Basque Country and Navarre have a distinct financial regime called "chartered regime"
       </li>
       <li>
        The Balearic Islands, the Basque Country, Catalonia, Galicia, Navarre, and the Valencian Community have a co-official language and therefore a distinct linguistic regime
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carreras_64-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-carreras-64">
          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Degree_of_financial_autonomy">
        Degree of financial autonomy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Degree of financial autonomy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Communities_of_chartered_regime" title="Communities of chartered regime">
