        Communities of chartered regime
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       How the communities are financed has been one of the most contentious aspects in their relationship with the central government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The constitution gave all communities significant control over spending, but the central government retained effective control of their revenue supply.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That is, the central government is still charge of levying and collecting most taxes, which it then redistributes to the autonomous communities with the aim of producing "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiscal_equalization" title="Fiscal equalization">
        fiscal equalization
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This applies to all communities, with the exception of the Basque Country and Navarre.
      </p>
      <p>
       This financial scheme is known as the "common regime". In essence, fiscal equalization implies that richer communities become net contributors to the system, while poorer communities become net recipients. The two largest net contributors to the system are the Balearic Islands and the Community of Madrid, in percentage terms, or the Community of Madrid and Catalonia in absolute terms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cinco_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cinco-71">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Central government funding is the main source of revenue for the communities of "common regime". Redistribution, or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_payments" title="Transfer payments">
        transfer payments
       </a>
       , are given to the communities of common regime to manage the responsibilities they have assumed. The amount they receive is based upon several calculations which include a consideration for population, land area, administrative units, dispersal of population, relative poverty, fiscal pressure and insularity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tanja_11-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-tanja-11">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The central government is committed to returning a specific percentage of taxes to all communities with common regime, within the differences allowed for fiscal equalization. The communities of common regime have the ability to add a surcharge to the so-called "ceded taxes"—taxes set at the central level, but collected locally—and they can lower or raise personal income taxes up to a limit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Basque Country and Navarre were granted an exception in the fiscal and financial system through the first additional disposition of the constitution that recognizes their historical "charters"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [viii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —hence they are known as "
       <a href="/wiki/Communities_of_chartered_regime" title="Communities of chartered regime">
        communities of chartered regime
       </a>
       " or "foral regime".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Through their "chartered regime", these communities are allowed to levy and collect all so-called "contracted taxes", including income tax and corporate tax, and they have much more flexibility to lower or raise them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This "chartered" or "foral" contract entails true financial autonomy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since they collect almost all taxes, they send to the central government a pre-arranged amount known as
       <i>
        cupo
       </i>
       , "quota" or
       <i>
        aportación
       </i>
       , "contribution", and the treaty whereby this system is recognized is known as
       <i>
        concierto
       </i>
       , "treaty", or
       <i>
        convenio
       </i>
       , "pact".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hacienda_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hacienda-73">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hence they are also said to have
       <i>
        concierto económico
       </i>
       , an "economic treaty". Since they collect all taxes themselves and only send a prearranged amount to the central government for the competences exclusive to the state, they do not participate in "fiscal equalization", in that they do not receive any money back.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spending">
        Spending
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Spending">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As more responsibilities have been assumed by the autonomous communities in areas such as social welfare, health, and education, public expenditure patterns have seen a shift from the central government towards the communities since the 1980s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the late 2000s, autonomous communities accounted for 35% of all public expenditure in Spain, a percentage that is even higher than that of states within a federation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With no legal constraints to balance budgets, and since the central government retains control over fiscal revenue in the communities of common regime, these are in a way encouraged to build up debt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Council_on_Fiscal_and_Financial_Policy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Council on Fiscal and Financial Policy (page does not exist)">
        Council on Fiscal and Financial Policy
       </a>
       , which includes representatives of the central government and of the autonomous communities, has become one of the most efficient institutions of coordination in matters of public expenditures and revenue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toboso_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-toboso-74">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Through the Council several agreements of financing have been agreed, as well as limits to the communities' public debt. The Organic Law of the Financing of Autonomous Communities of 1988 requires that the communities obtain the authorization of the central Ministry of Finance to issue public debt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toboso_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-toboso-74">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_regimes">
        Linguistic regimes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Linguistic regimes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BilingualSign_Spain.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="348" data-file-width="361" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BilingualSign_Spain.svg/220px-BilingualSign_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BilingualSign_Spain.svg/330px-BilingualSign_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BilingualSign_Spain.svg/440px-BilingualSign_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BilingualSign_Spain.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bilingual signs, showing the names of the city known as
         <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">
          Pamplona
         </a>
         in Spanish and Iruña in Basque
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The preamble to the constitution explicitly stated that it is the nation's will to protect "all Spaniards and the peoples of Spain in the exercise of human rights, their cultures and traditions, languages and institutions".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preamble_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-preamble-75">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is a significant recognition not only in that it differed drastically from the restrictive linguistic policies during the Franco era, but also because part of the distinctiveness of the "historical nationalities" lies on their own regional languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-villar_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-villar-12">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shabad_13-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-shabad-13">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The nation is thus openly multilingual,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conversi_18-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-conversi-18">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in which
       <a href="/wiki/Names_given_to_the_Spanish_language" title="Names given to the Spanish language">
        Castilian
       </a>
       —that is, Spanish—is the official language in all territories, but the "other Spanish languages" can also be official in their respective communities, in accordance with their Statutes of Autonomy.
      </p>
      <p>
       Article 3 of the constitution ends up declaring that the "richness of the distinct linguistic modalities of Spain represents a patrimony which will be the object of special respect and protection."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-third_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-third-76">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish remains the only official language of the state; other languages are only co-official with Spanish in the communities that have so regulated. In addition, knowledge of the Spanish language was declared a right and an obligation of all Spaniards.
      </p>
      <p>
       Spanish legislation, most notably in the Statutes of Autonomy of the bilingual communities, use the term "own language", or "language proper to a community",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [ix]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to refer to a language other than Spanish that originated or had historical roots in that particular territory. The Statutes of Autonomy of the respective autonomous communities have declared
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       the language proper to the Basque Country and Navarre,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       the language proper to Catalonia, the Balearic Islands and the Valencian Community—where it is historically, traditionally and officially known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">
        Valencian
       </a>
       —and
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       to be the language proper to Galicia. There are other protected regional languages in other autonomous communities. As a percentage of total population in Spain,
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       is spoken by 2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       by 17%, and
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       by 7% of all Spaniards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-78">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable hlist" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: auto; text-align: left; font-size: 100%;">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">
        Subdivisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">
        Provinces of Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">
        Municipalities of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Comarcas_of_Spain" title="Comarcas of Spain">
        Comarcas of Spain
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Spanish constitution recognizes the municipalities
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [x]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and guarantees their autonomy. Municipal, or city, councils
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [xi]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are in charge of the municipalities' government and administration, and they are integrated by a mayor
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [xii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and councillors,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [xiii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the latter elected by universal suffrage, and the former elected either by the councillor or by suffrage.
      </p>
      <p>
       Provinces
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [xiv]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are groups of municipalities and recognized by the constitution. Their competences and institutions of government vary greatly among communities. In all communities which have more than one province, provinces are governed by
       <i>
        "provincial deputations"
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        "provincial councils"
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [xv]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a limited scope of administrative competences.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Basque Country, the provinces, renamed as "
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Historical_territories&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Historical territories (page does not exist)">
        historical territories
       </a>
       ",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lurraldeak_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-lurraldeak-37">
         [iv]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are governed by "chartered deputations"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [xvi]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —with assume the competences of a provincial deputation as well as the fiscal powers of their "
       <a href="/wiki/Communities_of_chartered_regime" title="Communities of chartered regime">
        chartered regime
       </a>
       "—and by "General Juntas"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [xvii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —parliaments with legislative powers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Canary Islands and the Balearic Islands, each major island is governed by an "insular council".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [xviii]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Catalonia, the "provincial deputations" have very little power, as other territorial subdivisions have been created.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_52-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-smith-52">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In those seven autonomous communities formed by a single province, the provincial deputations have been replaced by the communities' institutions of government; in fact, the provinces themselves are not only coterminous with the communities, but correspond in essence to the communities themselves. The two-tier territorial organization common to most communities—first province, then municipalities—is therefore non-existent in these "uniprovincial" communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiscal_6-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-fiscal-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable hlist" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: auto; text-align: left; font-size: 100%;">

         </a>

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Castell%C3%B3n" title="Province of Castellón">

         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Valencia" title="Province of Valencia">
          Valencia
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The constitution also allows the creation of other territorial entities formed by groups of municipalities. One of such territorial subdivision is the
       <i>
        comarca
       </i>
       (equivalent of a "district", "shire" or "county"). While all communities have unofficial historical, cultural or natural
       <i>
        comarcas
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [xix]
        </a>
       </sup>
       only in Aragon and Catalonia they have been legally recognized as territorial entities with administrative powers (see
       <a href="/wiki/Comarcal_council" title="Comarcal council">
        comarcal councils
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [xx]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Competences_of_the_autonomous_governments">
        Competences of the autonomous governments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Autonomous_communities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Competences of the autonomous governments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The competences of the autonomous communities are not homogeneous.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Broadly the competences are divided into "Exclusive", "Shared" and "Executive". In some cases the autonomous community may have exclusive responsibility for the administration of a policy area but may only have executive (i.e.,carries out) powers as far as the policy itself is concerned, meaning it must enforce policy and laws decided at the national level.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable hlist" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: auto; text-align: left; font-size: 100%;">

           </span>
           ,
          </li>
          <li>
           Catalan:
           <i>
            <span lang="ca">
             <i>
              Comunitat autònoma
             </i>
            </span>
           </i>
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
             [kumuniˈtat əwˈtɔnumə]
            </a>
           </span>
           <ul>
            <li>
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

              </a>
             </span>
             (in Valencian)
            </li>

          </li>

          </a>
          .
         </span>
